<li>An entrepreneur is a person who identifies a business opportunity, harnesses and obtains the resources necessary to initiate a successful business activity.</li>
<li>Entrepreneurship is the act or process of identifying business opportunities and gathering the necessary resources to initiate a successful business activity</li>
<li>Difference between self-employment and salaried employment</li>
</ul>
<p>In salaried employment, a person has a guaranteed income and other benefits while in self-employment, a person has no guaranteed income and there are more expenses to cover.</p>

</li>

<li>☐ Elimination / Reduction of poverty: reduce rural-urban migration</li>
<li>☐ Provision of opportunities for employment and personal advancement</li>
<li>☐ Trying to narrow the income differences between the rich and the poor.</li>
</ul>
<p>i) Employment Creation:</p>
<p>ii) Promotion of National Productivity: This is through production of goods and services with the country and therefore the growth of the Gross Domestic Product (GDP)</p>

<p>iv) Conservation of foreign Exchange: Entrepreneurs produce goods and services that are needed by people and reduction in importing those goods and hence the governments' save foreign exchange.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-function-of-an-entrepreneur">The Function of an Entrepreneur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-function-of-an-entrepreneur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) The bearing of uncertainty is the primary function of the entrepreneur. Closes or profits
ii) The management of the business enterprise is a candele date
iii) Provision of risk capital and invention.
iv) Identifying gaps in the market and turning such gap to business opportunities. Etoinitiate a business.
v) Financing the businesses, through raising and mobilizing the necessary resources to exploit opportunity.
vi) Searching for business opportunities through environmental scans.
vii) Mobilization of resources needed to start and run a business e.g. from</p>
<p>a) Personals' savings
b) Friends &amp; relatives
c) Financial institutions.</p>
<p>viii) Evaluation of business opportunities to access viability and any other benefits that might accrue to the business.
ix) Provide the necessary leadership for the business and those working in it.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="entrepreneurship-the-evolution-of-entrepreneurship-in-kenya">ENTREPRENEURSHIP The Evolution of Entrepreneurship in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurship-the-evolution-of-entrepreneurship-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Interest in the development of entrepreneurship and small enterprise in Kenya gained momentum as a possible remedy to the stagnation of economic development and the escalating unemployment problem between the early 1960 and 1970s</li>
<li>Although there were attempts by the government to develop entrepreneurship, the main impetus came from the international labor organization (ILO) report.</li>
<li>The report centered on the potential of the informal sector and suggested that the bulk of Kenya's urban workers were self-employed in small enterprises.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychological-theory">Psychological theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychological-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The focus is that entrepreneurs have unique values, attitudes and need which drive them.</li>
<li>People’s behavior results from their attempt to stop striving for unique needs and values.</li>
<li>The psychological school focus is on personality factors believing that entrepreneurs have unique values and attitudes towards work and life.</li>
<li>Among the most frequent traits of entrepreneurs include the need for achievement, Locus of Control and Risk taking propensity.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="658cd14f">Maslow’s Need Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#658cd14f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Theory of human needs is identified with the psychologist Abraham Maslow. This theory is based on three specific assumptions:</p>
<ol>
<li>The human beings are never satisfied. Their wants are determined by what they have. When people are hungry or thirsty, the quest for food or water influences how they behave. However if food and water is acquired, the same person will want something else, perhaps as a feplaceto live in or asocial status.</li>
<li>A satisfied need does not cause behavior. Once people satisfy their need for safety, they are motivated by yet unsatisfied needs, not the ones that are satisfied,</li>
<li>Human needs are arranged in hierarchy of importance. These needs range from low level biological (physiological) need to such high level needs to asself-actualization.</li>
</ol>

<p>THE ENTREPRENEUR</p>
<p>Types of Entrepreneurs</p>
<p>e) Craft entrepreneurs</p>
<p>Exploits and utilizes personal skill to start a business without thinking of its growth or the expansion of a business.
Often, most than not in this type of entrepreneur, i.e. there is no expanding even after a long time, it is not a business expansion oriented. This skills can be technical skills, professional skill, etc.</p>
<p>f) Opportunistic entrepreneurs</p>
<p>This is a person who starts a business, acts as a manager and with a view to expand the business to maximum.
Hemight, not haveth, skill or profession, but he has the opportunity to start and direct others.
Hesees beyond and has abilitiest o initiate and venture into business that will expand and grow.
He is innovative, i.e. somebody able to delegate activities to others, ready and able to see, scan the environment.</p>
<p>g) Social entrepreneur</p>
<p>Recognizes as social problem and uses entrepreneurial principles to organize, create and manage a venture to achieve a social change.</p>
<p>h) Political entrepreneur</p>
<p>Is a business person who utilizes political systems or seeks support from political bodies in order to promote, expand and profit from their own commercial ventures.
A political player whose ekstremity and intention to initiate and venture the company is the common goods that can be shared by an organized general public.</p>

<p>✓ New technological developments have created opportunities for those with the right technical expertise</p>
<p>f) Concept Multipliers
✓ Someone who identifies as successful concept that can be duplicated by other seg</p>
<p>g) Acquirer:
✓ Those who take over abusiness started by others and use their own idea to make it successful</p>
<p>h) Buy/Sell artists: those who buy a company for the purpose of improving it before selling it for a profit.</p>
<p>i) Economy of Scale exploiters: Those who benefit from large volume of sales by offering discount prices and operating with low overheads.</p>
<p>j) Inventors: Those with particular inventive abilities who design a better product and then create a companion to develop, produce and sell their em.</p>
<p>k) Self-employed: individuals who perform all the work and keep all the profit.</p>
<p>l) Speculator/Value: Those individuals who buy property at a low price with the anticipation that prices will go up and sell at a higher price.</p>
<p>m) Conglomerate: an entrepreneur who builds up a portfolio of ownership in small businesses, sometimes using shares or assets of one company to provide the financial base to acquire another.</p>
<p>n) Matriarch or patriarch: The head of family owned business who often employs several members of the family.</p>

<p>Factorsto considerin startingabusiness</p>
<p>a) PersonalFactors</p>
<p>i. Personalabilities</p>
<p>One must have personality traits that will enable him/her to start, continue and succeed in business. One must have entrepreneurial traits and bemotivated and determined to succeed in business. E.g. one must be willing to work hard and pursue his/her goals persistently; he/she must be innovative, creative and optimistic.</p>
<p>ii. Skills: Oneneedstohavethetrainingandexperiencenecessaryintheproposedlineof</p>

<p>business.He/
shemusthaveadequateknowledgeaboutproductorserviceandthenecessarymanagerial skills for the business to succeed.</p>
<p>iii. Interests / hobbies: As an entrepreneur, how much interests does one have in line of his/her business? Ann interest or hobby can be a basis for a business.
iv. Family: Small businesses and family are inseparable, one affect the other. You need to consider possible effects of the business on the family and how the family could affect the business.
v. Health: Running a business successfully calls for a lot of hard work. It involves a lot of physical and mental energies. If an entrepreneur has failing health, it is advisable to engage in less strenuous activities.</p>
<p>b) Resource Factors</p>
<p>i.) Financial Resources: These include money saved by the entrepreneur and money that may be borrowed from individuals and institutions like banks, buildings, societies, cooperatives, etctostart and run abusiness.
ii.) Labor Resources: The availability and suitability of labor should be assessed.
iii.) Equipment/Machinery: Tools of the trade that are essential in any business. They may include furniture, office equipment, machine for a specific job, etc.
iv.) Raw Materials: These are items that are to be converted to states that can be readily used by consumers. These include timber, fone is furniture business, clothematerial is fin dress making business.</p>
<p>c) Environmental factors</p>
<p>i.) Location: Factors such as community profile, communication, road, water, safety, source of raw materials and competitions should be considered when locating a business. This enables easy access to both the business by customers.
ii.) Government Policies / regulations: Policies such as taxation, pricing, licensing, loans and policy documents affect small enterprises. Information on the above is available from district Information Offices, Trade Organizations, Kenya Chamber of Commerce and Government Printers. iii.) Infrastructure: Availability of roads, power, water and telephones or excess are very important in some types of business.
iv.) The economy of the society: The average income and employment trends determine the demand for goods and services within the community to sell product or services at reduced profits, as trong economy creates ample demand and good profits.
v.) Competition: An entrepreneur should try to assess the number of competitors in his or her environment in order to compete with them successful.
vi.) Market: A market for the product or services is very important to the entrepreneur. One has to assess whether there's a steady market.
vii.) Community and Culture: The entrepreneur has to consider:</p>
<p>a) General Customer: An entrepreneur should try to assess the number of competitors in his or her environment in order to compete with them successfully.
b) The mix of politics
c) Taboos/belief: SegMuslims cannot operate any business dealing with pork products
d) Traditions peculiar to his/her community</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="creativity-and-innovation">CREATIVITY AND INNOVATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#creativity-and-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Creativity refers to the process of devising an ew idea, or this that results in the improved efficiency or effectiveness of a system.</li>
<li>☑ Innovation means improving an existing idea or thing. Commercializing of an idea or turning idea into an opportunity.</li>
<li>☑ Innovation builds on creativity when something new, tangible and value-creating is developed from the ideas.</li>
<li>☑ Innovation turns new concepts into realities, creating a wealth and power.</li>
<li>☑ Creativity and control. Innovation makes long-standing arrangement of sole te and frees resources to be employed elsewhere leading to greater economic efficiency. E.g. computerization.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-for-opposing-innovation">Reasons for Opposing Innovation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-opposing-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) The entrepreneur stands to have a practical concern that unforeseen innovation may cause a disaster. e.g. side effects. e.g. of a drug.
ii) Fear of losing profits in the event innovation does not translate to the expectations.
iii) Where the entrepreneur held a monopoly position in the market, there is fear of losing authority and control.
iv) Fear of upsetting the moral and social value of demand for the product.
v) Desire to preserve the existing market confidence.
vi) Fear of upsetting tradition in production management and market scope.
vii) Fear of opening a loophole to competition hence loss of business grip.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-for-innovation">Reasons for Innovation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Innovation is essential for the entrepreneur in solving the inefficiency problems.</li>
<li>☑ As a means of cost reduction and imposings a significant social and market grip.</li>
<li>☑ Profit improvements are looked at from the innovation point of view through new technology in management and production.</li>
<li>☑ To encounter competition by already established businesses.</li>
<li>☑ To facilitate the opening up of new markets both locally and internationally.</li>
<li>☑ To facilitate the diversification of productrisks and losses. Toprotect current position of monopolys.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="requirement-for-innovation">Requirement for Innovation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirement-for-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i.) Economic demand</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ People engage in innovation out of belief that the economic return will be greater than its costs.
ii.) Surplus capital</li>
<li>☑ Provides the necessary time and startup costs for implementing an ew idea.
iii.) Ability to assemble and invest capital.
iv.) Mobile capital which is stable.</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ Capital cannot serve unless it can move to potential innovator unless it can move to allow the various types of wealth to be created e.g. title deeds – stability is provided by aruleoflaw.</p>
<p>v.) Availability of growth- fostering social institutions which facilitate the speed of technological advancement. vi.) Ability and willingness to think and act creativity (Entrepreneurs) I.e. the philosophical and psychological requirements.</p>
<p>vii.) Geographical and other circumstantial causes such as ethical issues.</p>
<p>✓ Societies in which innovation is seen as a sinful or people are punished or are shunned to think differently than others are unlikely to experience innovation.</p>
<p>viii.) The size of the firm.</p>
<p>✓ Large firms have the advantage of introducing innovation since they can afford it. ☐ They tend to attract more talents employees to advice on new ideas.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="entrepreneurial-culture">Entrepreneurial Culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurial-culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Refer to the way of embracing the concept of finding new opportunities in business and gathering the necessary resources to fill the opportunity.</p>
<p>✓ Many governments around the world want to promote entrepreneurship because they have recognized the importance of entrepreneurship.</p>
<p>✓ In other words, entrepreneurship is a way of people embarrassing life by participating in activities that enable them to create new business enterprises.</p>
<p>✓ A country can develop the entrepreneurial culture by forming policies that constitute the following:</p>
<p>☐ Integration of entrepreneurship training in the overall educations system to take you on you</p>
<p>☐ Exposure of entrepreneurship to those who look potential to actual business practices and activities through the networks and business contacts of rule models.</p>
<p>☐ Creation of a conducive and enabling environment that permits new business to immerge and flourish.</p>
<p>✓ The creation of entrepreneurial culture has to come from deep social convictions based on strong values and systems of the locals</p>
<p>✓ It should be created in a way that it welcomes entrepreneurship and respects their own or the industry's future values</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="theprocessof-screeningabusinessidea">TheProcessof ScreeningaBusinessIdea.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theprocessof-screeningabusinessidea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ After generating business ideas- it is important that some evaluation through a screeningprocessbemade.
☑ The screening process is a systematic evaluation ideas in order to select the best ideawhichwould suit one.
☑ Thescreeningprocessmustbedonecarefully,objectively,soberlyandwithoutanyemotions.
☑ The business idea screening is required even when there is only one idea to consider. Thisis because this is a stage of starting a business that may be not be profitable or may bedifficultto run
☑ Thescreeningprocessmustthereforeevaluatethefollowing</p>
<p>a) PersonalEvaluation</p>
<ul>
<li>theobjectiveforgoingto business</li>
<li>personalinterests</li>
<li>Thedegreeofcommitmenttothebusinessorotherse.g.family.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) PersonalSkills</p>
<ul>
<li>TheselfSWOTanalysis-thisaimsatanalyzingones</li>
</ul>
<p>a. Strengths
b. Weaknesses
c. Opportunities
d. Treats</p>
<ul>
<li>"Strengths" and "Weaknesses" should focus on the internal environment(management,product/service),whilst"Opportunities"and"Threats"should focusontheexternalenvironment (economy,market andcompetitors).</li>
<li>Clearly, it is important that your business idea has significant strengths (or candevelopment)andaplan tocountertoanyweaknesses.Yourbusinessideashould bedevelopedtotakeadvantageof anyopportunitiesandthoughtshouldbegiventohowyou wouldrespond to threats.</li>
<li>ASWOTanalysisshouldprovideprooftoyou,yourinvestorsandfunderset.,ofthe likelihood of your business succeeding or failing. If your analysis suggests itwillfailyou needto reconsideryouridea.</li>
</ul>
<p>Thescreeningprocessorevaluationhelpsidentify;</p>
<p>☐ Strengths:E.g.Distinctivecompetence,Adequatefinances,Accesstoeconomiesofscale, Goodinnovation ability, provenmanagement</p>

<p>☐ Weakness: E.g. Lackofkeyskill, Internal operations problems, Low morale, Poortrack records, Weak internal image
☐ Opportunities: E.g. Potential customers, Potential goodwill, Afavorablesocial environment
☐ Threats: Strong competitions, Adverse government policies, Political instability, mismanaged economy, Unfavorable legislation</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-good-business-idea">Characteristics of a Good Business idea.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-good-business-idea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Easy to manage and involve minimal risk. ii) Does not require excessive capital investments. iii) Offers a good return on capital. iv) The idea has scope for growth, expansion and diversification. v) Comparative with owner's goal and interest. vi) Not against expectation of the society. v) Has a short gestation period. vi) Easy to exit when necessary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-sources-of-new-ideas">The sources of new ideas<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-sources-of-new-ideas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition-of-a-business-opportunity">Definition of a Business Opportunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-a-business-opportunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Abusiness opportunity may be defined as an attractive project idea. Which an entrepreneur accepts for investment on the basis of what is known about the possible success for the project.</p>
<p>☑ Are a business opportunity can by distinguish from an emergency facility through the following two ingredients.</p>
<p>i. A good marketscope</p>
<p>ii. An attractive return on investment</p>
<p>(profit) Qualities (Characteristics) of a Good Business Opportunity:</p>
<p>The following are qualities of a good business opportunity.</p>
<p>a. Demand – there should exist a good marketscope
b. Return on investment – i. the business should be sufficiently profitable.
c. Availability of raw materials
d. Enough skilled people.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="evaluation-of-a-business-opportunities-objectives-of-a-pre-feasibility-study">Evaluation of a Business Opportunities (objectives of a pre-feasibility study)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation-of-a-business-opportunities-objectives-of-a-pre-feasibility-study" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Once a business opportunity has been identified, one needs to confirm that it is viable through a pre-feasibility study.</p>
<p>☑ The main objective of a feasibility study is to determine whether.</p>
<p>a. a heinvestment opportunity is promising enough
b. The project is viable from the marketing manufacturing and other pointsof view.
c. Any aspect of the project that may be crucial to call for in depth analysis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-purpose-of-a-pre-feasibility-study-market-research">The Purpose of a Pre-feasibility Study (Market Research)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-purpose-of-a-pre-feasibility-study-market-research" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i.) To verify that the investment opportunity is promising enough to make a firm decision.ii.) To confirm that the project is viable from the</p>
<p>a. Marketing
b. Manufacturing and
c. Other pointsof view.iii.) To identify any aspect of the project that is critical or crucial enough to call for in depth analysis</p>
<p>iv.) To acquire comprehensive technical, economic and commercial data for the final investment decision.</p>
<p>v.) To enable an in-depth study of aspect such as</p>
<p>Market potential, Technical requirements, Managerial ability, financial projections and analysis, Risks evaluation, Business environment analysis.vi.) To enable sourcing reliable information such as</p>
<p>a. Authorized publications
b. Consultant’s openings.</p>
<p>vii.) To establish the final outcome of whether or not to proceed with the business.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="business-incubation">Business Incubation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#business-incubation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Business incubation is the process of nurturing small and start-up initiatives or business storeletive maturity to become self-sustaining business, healthy and wealth-generating entities.</p>
<p>Downloaded by dspop Service Delivery (<a href="mailto:dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ The failure rate of anystart-up business stands at 90% globally.
✓ The main causes of business failure;</p>
<p>Page 27 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by dspop Service Delivery (<a href="mailto:dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i) Insufficient capital for start-up. ii) Insufficient knowledge of business and industry. iii) Lack of Entrepreneurial and business skills. iv) Lack of Managerial skills. v) Inadequate Training. vi) Lack of credit facilities. vii) Lack of markets. viii) Insufficient knowledge of markets. <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-incubation-process">The Incubation Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-incubation-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ The business incubation programmes are designed to accelerate success for future pre-neural companies through an awareness of support resources and services.
✓ Incubators vary in the way they deliver their services in their organizational structure and in the types of clients they serve.
✓ Business incubators differ from research and technology in their dedication to start-up and early stage businesses.
✓ Research and Technology institutes tend to be large scale projects that house everything from corporate government or university labs to very small companies.
✓ The research institutions don’t offer business assistance services which are the main objective of business incubation.
✓ Unlike many business assistance programmes, business incubators don’t serve any and all companies.
✓ Entrepreneurs who may wish to enter a business incubation program must apply for admission.
✓ Acceptance criteria vary from program to program but in general only those with feasible businesses is and workable businesses plan are admitted.
✓ The time a company spends in an incubation programme vary widely depending on a number of factors, including the type of business and the Entrepreneur’s level of business expertise.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="entrepreneurial-motivation">ENTREPRENEURIAL MOTIVATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurial-motivation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

iii. Need for Power: Need to exercise power over others and need to control others. People with a high need for power have a greater concern for exercising influence and control.
iv. Need for Recognition: We normally strive to get recognition about our achievement in life, by our peers, family and society. If you aspire to be recognized, then this could be an important drive for you to go into self-employment.
v. Need for Security: All menthrivetobefree from anxiety:
☐ Anxiety about our very survival

☐ Anxiety about the future, both for ourselves
as well as for our families. It is for this reason that we all strive to maximize our returns, wage employment may not meet this anxiety especially if we are not pensionable.
vi. Self-actualization need:
Refers to the need to accomplish that which you as a person is capable of achieving, the need to be unique. Through entrepreneurial activities and with dedication and commitment, you can realize this need, an ed that is</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maslow-s-need-theory">Maslow's Need Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maslow-s-need-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Theory of human needs is identified with the psychologist Abraham Maslow. This theory is based on threespecific assumptions:</p>
<ol>
<li>That human beings are never satisfied. Their wants are determined by what they have. When people are hungry or thirsty, the quest for food or water influences how they behave. However if food and water is acquired, the same person will want something else, perhaps a safe place to live in or a social status.</li>
<li>A satisfied need does not cause behavior. Once people satisfy their need for safety, they are motivated by yet unsatisfied needs, not the ones – that is unsatisfied,</li>
<li>Human needs are arranged in hierarchy of importance. These needs range from low level biological (physiological) needs to such high level needs as self-actualization.</li>
</ol>
<p>Physiological Needs: The need for Food, Clothing Shelter. They are required for survival. Werequire money to satisfy these basic needs. If we do not have any source of income and cannot get wage employment, we may be motivated to entrepreneurship.</p>
<p>Safety or security needs: Once or basic needs are satisfied, our behavior is no longer motivated by them. At this point we begin to worry about the security or safety of our families, etheneed to be free from physical danger and fear of loss of job. For entrepreneurs, since their ability to</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-969d690d.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Page 33 of 165</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by dspop Service Delivery (<a href="mailto:dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>cater for these needs depend on how hard they work, these needs will motivate their behavior. Theysavemoneyto usein thecaseofillness, purchaseofinsurancepolicies.</p>
<p><strong>Belongingness Need (Affiliation or acceptance needs):</strong> Once safety needs are satisfied, they nolonger motivate us to work harder. Since we are social beings, we need to belong, to be acceptedbyothers likefamily,work groups,mentors.</p>
<p><strong>Esteem needs:</strong> They are more abstract than physiological, safety and belonging needs. This kind ofneedsproducessuch satisfactionas; Power,Prestige, Status,self-confidence.</p>
<p><strong>Self-Actualization Needs:</strong> Means making the most of what we have to maximize our potential. They want to achieve the best and believe that no one is better than them. They aspire for a standardofexcellence.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leading-and-motivating-others">Leading and Motivating Others<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leading-and-motivating-others" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As an entrepreneur success, depend on how you motivate your employees. The following techniques should be employed:</p>
<p>i. Built workers self-esteem: By praising the good work done by your employees, you are building confidence in selves. Appreciate what they have done.</p>
<p>ii. Inform employees: Tell yourself what you are trying to accomplish.</p>
<p>iii. Delegation of authority and responsibility: Good delegation will allow you as a leader to devote more time to important and crucial issues within your business.</p>
<p>iv. Maintain contact: Know your staff well enough by maintaining personal contact.</p>
<p>v. Apply reinforcement principal: You should reward behaviors that you consider desirable because people tend to repeat rewarded behavior. Don’t reward undesirable behavior as people tend not to repeat unrewarded behavior.</p>
<p>vi. Be an active listener: By active listening, you will be an effective communicator which is an important quality of a leader. Your employees will take it that you appreciate them and have concern in them.</p>
<p>vii. Sets specific goals: Sets specific clearly understood measurable goals and continuously review them.</p>
<p>viii. Take collective action: When you must deal with some negative aspects of a worker’s performance, you should talk to that worker in private, never criticize a worker in public.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sources-of-influence-in-leadership">Sources of influence in Leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-influence-in-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Legitimate Authority: A person may gain compliance from sub-ordinates because of the authority which is associated with the office the person holds. The power of the office is often derived from the person's responsibilities as a manager, administrator or politician. Owners of business enterprises enjoy the power to reward, reprimand or punish their subordinates.</p>
<p>b) Economic Power: the clout that comes with economic might sometimes referred to as reward power. So a person who is in a position to administer economic rewards, couldn't fluecethebehaviorof subordinatesthroughappointmentsordenialofsuchrewards.</p>
<p>c) Coercive Power: a person who is in a position to get other people to do things by the use of force or threats and intimidation is said to possess coercive involuntary action where the subordinates submit their consent only because they fear the repercussions of punishment or violence.</p>
<p>d) Persuasion; There are times when persons in positions of responsibility need to use witandsweet words in order to get things done through others.</p>
<p>e) Referent power: Is based on the subordinate's identification with the leader. The leader exercises influence because of perceived attractiveness, personal character, reputation or what is called "charisma". E.g. doctors, athletes, academicians, wealthy people. This respect could be turned into a source of influence for those who admire a particular person.</p>
<p>f) Expert Power.</p>
<p>Theories of</p>
<p>Leadershipa) Trait Theory</p>
<ul>
<li>Assumethatleaders are born not made.</li>
<li>Leadership consists of certain inherited characteristics or personality traits which distinguish leaders from followers. E.g. need for achievement, focus, assertiveness, etc. b) Situational Theory</li>
<li>Leadership is considered to be a function of the situation which a leader emerges and works. It is based on assumption that leadership is basically situational.</li>
<li>The person who becomes the leader of the work group is thought to be the person who knows best what to do and seen by the group as the most suitable leader in the particular situation</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Behavioral Theory</p>
<ul>
<li>It is based on the assumption that leadership effectiveness depends upon what the leader does. The leadership behavior is the product of the leader and the followers.</li>
<li>A leader uses his skills to exercise influence and modify behavior of his subordinates. Qualities of a leader: Should have energy, perseverance, education-up-to-date, intelligent, personality, creative, innovative, optimistic, balanced, objective, enthusiastic</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-of-decision-making">Method of Decision Making<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-of-decision-making" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are several methods you can use to make business decisions, among them we have:</p>
<p>i. Rule of Thumb: A decision is made based on existing established procedures e.g. based on laws, customs, religion, etc. You can't change
ii. Committee Approach/Teamwork: It's where using a selected number of people from the main group to make a decision which will be accepted by all.
iii. Critical Path Analysis: This is making decision stage by stage until the final decision is reached.
iv. Brainstorming: This is where all members of a group develop ideas for a solution
v. Problems solving Chart
vi. Solution Evaluation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="form-of-step-of-the-decision-making-process">Form of Step of the Decision Making process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#form-of-step-of-the-decision-making-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Identify the major problem e.g. low productivity</li>
<li>Determine major causes of the problem e.g. low salaries, poor working conditions</li>
<li>Determine potential solutions — how to solve</li>
<li>Evaluate potential solutions</li>
<li>Select the best solution</li>
<li>Implement the solution</li>
<li>Verify the solution. Problem Solving Chart</li>
</ol>
<p>☑ You can use a problem solving chart as one way of organizing possible solutions to the problems.
☑ After completing it you will be able to analyze alternative solutions in terms of potential advantages disadvantages and consequences. A space is provided on the chart for four possible solutions.</p>

✓ Listing potential advantages will indicate how each potential disadvantage will illustrate how the potential solution will adversely affect you.
✓ In some instances, an advantage or disadvantage may be the same for two or more alternatives.
✓ Potential consequences you identify in the last column will be the result of analyzing the potential advantages and disadvantages.
✓ The y should equal the potential net result of implementing a particular solution.
✓ The problem solving chart can help you to analyze and solve major problems which would otherwise have an adverse effect on your business.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solution-evaluation-form">Solution Evaluation Form<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-evaluation-form" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Another procedure for analyzing potential solutions is to identify reasons for an address as against each potential solution.
✓ To use the solution evaluation form to the best advantage, you should:</p>
<ol>
<li>Write a brief description of the problem at the top of the form.</li>
<li>Write a brief description of the proposed solution.</li>
<li>In the reasons for column, list important factors which would favour implementing the proposed solution.</li>
<li>In the reasons against column, list important factors for not implementing the proposed solutions.</li>
<li>Rate each factor by its importance to you. The numerical ratings might be 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 where a low rating of 1 indicates that the factor affects the problem only slightly and a high rating of 5 indicates that the factor is extremely important in making your decision. Each factor in the reason for column and each factor in the reason against column would receive an numerical rating.</li>
<li>Add the ratings in each of the two rating columns, the column with a higher total will give you some indication of the potential for a particular solution. If there is a big difference between the two totals (in favor of reasons for the solution) you may feel more secure in the use of this technique to make a decision. If there is little difference in totals for both columns, it might indicate that you need additional information about the problem.</li>
</ol>

<p>✓ Change is the need to make or become different, to replace or improve, to reform or reorganize to fit to the current situation which results in higher productivity or performance. ☐ Is a systematic planned effort to improve effectiveness of the business. Change is risky, uncertain ☐ As an entrepreneur, you play a key role of managing change in your business.</p>

<p>NeedforChange</p>
<p>a) Thereis need to adopt/adapt
b) Toremain viable (economically)
c) Wewant growth (sales + profit), employees, customers (increasemarketshare), diversity
d) Enhance chances of survival (Change before Change changes you).</p>
<p>Reasons for change</p>
<p>a) People change because they are dissatisfied with the status quo.
b) Interdepartmental conflicts – conflicts in departments
c) Thereed to cut costs
d) Toneed to improve efficiency
e) Need for company or personal security
f) Existence of an ew demand in the market
g) Tough international and national competition
h) Change into the only category</p>
<p>These conditions create threats and present opportunities in an organization. Factorsthat influence change in your business</p>
<p>a) Economic activities: e.g. changes in the prices of some input
b) Competition: The competitors' activities; bewatch fulon competition to responge in good time; e.g. by aggressive advertising, reducing the price
c) The government and political environment: New policies, regulations relating to taxation and remuneration policies
d) Technology: For adaptability and business growth. Go for the new technology
e) Educational and social factors: e.g. your customers' changes in education status, taste, family size, status, age, sex, population distribution</p>
<p>The above call for change in terms of quality, price, promptness, indelivery, packaging, labelling of your product etc.</p>
<p>Types of change:</p>
<p>a) Change of Product: e.g. you change your products' labelling, size, packaging, color, taste, quality, smell
b) Change of service: change in terms of promptness (quick/fastness) and quality service
c) Change of technology: e.g. Tools and equipment, material, technical skills, procedures, production methods
d) Change of policy: Change of objectives, goals and policies to follow to meet government policies.</p>
<p>Why People Resist Change</p>
<ol>
<li>Fear of the unknown (don't know what next)</li>
<li>Misinformation (false information), no information at all, no communication</li>
</ol>

b) Measures the profit cost and revenue elements.
c) Affects the product quality and quantity
d) Has a psychological impact on consumers. iii) The placement – also known as distribution is concerned with linking the seller and buyer through the product and involves elements of a) Inform potential customers
b) To convince and persuade existing customer to continue or choose the product
c) To establish a business image or goodwill
d) To canter competition from other business dealings
e) To increase sales and revenue.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-marketing-mix">The Marketing Mix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-marketing-mix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The term marketing mix refers to the apportionment of effort, combinations, designing and integration of allelement sof marketing into a single programme aimed at achieving the objective of a business enterprise.</li>
<li>It is a detailed strategy, tasks, operations policies programmes, techniques and activities to which resources may be allocated to achieve marketing objectives.</li>
<li>The term is used to describe the combination of the four inputs which constitute a marketing system (4 pcs) i.e. ☐ The product</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-4ps-the-four-ps">The 4Ps (the four Ps)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-4ps-the-four-ps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The marketing mix denotes a combination of the various elements which in their totality make up a marketing system i.e. the product, the price, the placement and the promotion.</p>

<li>The product element of the marketing mix strives to establish. A product policy The product strategies The product mix</li>

<ul>
<li>Pricing the product is an important element of the marketing mix.</li>
<li>Price is the value of a market or service to meet the customer satisfaction. The product involves: i) Profits – through price profit cost and revenue elements are measurable. ii.) Product quality – price gives indication of the product quality. iii.) Profits – through price profit cost and revenue elements are measurable. iv.) Product quality – price gives indication of the product quality. - co-operate goals – are achievable through pricing decisions especially in formulating marketing strategies. vi.) Meeting consumer expectations is measurable through price.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-sole-proprietorship">Disadvantages of Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Limited life in case of death of the owner</li>
<li>Unlimited liability may cause the owner to lose his original property</li>
<li>The sole proprietor serves as losed entirely by himself</li>
<li>Limited capital may delay expansion.</li>
<li>Working for longer hours may result to fatigue</li>
<li>Lack of essential skills may cause mis-management.</li>
</ol>

<p>ProblemstheSoleProprietorship mayface.</p>

<li>Lack of skills, may lead to mis-management</li>
<li>Working for longer hours, may lead to fatigue</li>
<li>Loses are served by the owner</li>
<li>Limited capital to facilitate expansion functions.</li>
<li>Lack of consultancy, may lead to poor decision making</li>
<li>Unlimited liability, may cause lose of property.</li>
</ol>
<p>Partnership</p>
<p>✓ According to the partnership Act. A partnership is referred to as a relationship which subsists between persons carrying on a business in common with a view of making profits.
✓ A partnership is thus an extension of sole proprietorship and is in fact necessitated by the fact that a sole trader may for several reasons fail to carry out his business efficiently and profitability.
✓ Partnerships with the financial and managerial skill to get their interest to make profit.</p>
<p>Formation</p>
<p>✓ According to the partnership Act (934), a partnership business may come into existence through a payoff before following ways.
i) Orally
ii) By action of persons concerned
By a simple put in written
iv) By a partnership deed</p>
<p>NB the above way soforming a partnership are allowed by the partnership Act. However its better to remember that it may be made illegal under the following circumstances.</p>
<p>Circumstances under which the Partnership is illegal</p>
<p>✓ If the partnership has been formed for an illegal purpose, e.g. theft.
If it is formed and the partnership contains more than 20 members</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="features-characteristicsofapartnership">Features/characteristicsofaPartnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-characteristicsofapartnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Mutual agency – each partner is an agent of the partnership and therefore any action by one partner with transacting the business binds the rest of the partners provided his actions are with inthe partners express or implied authority.</li>
<li>Limited life – since the partnership is a relationship originating from an agreement between two or more members any changes in their relationship caused by factors such as death with drawal of a partner e.t. c. terminated the partnership or dissolves it.</li>
<li>Unlimited liability</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>In a partnership the partners’ liability is not limited to the amount of capital investment.</li>
<li>The partners are separately held liable for the debt so f. business and their personal properties may be sold to meet such debts.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>
<p>Ownership of interests – the interest of a partner in a partnership business e.g. rights to inspect the accounting records of a firm of a firm, admission or dismissal of partner’s transit of a partnership, the partnership.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sharing of profits</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Each partner’s share of profits is proportional to his/her investment in the partnership. And any agreement of non-partner to share the profits does not make an on-partner a partner.</p>
<p>NB circumstances under which a non-partner may be included in sharing the partnership profits and losses.</p>
<ol>
<li>As compensation for services rendered to the partnership</li>
<li>As compensation for the partnership use of his/her property or name.</li>
<li>As payment for loans advanced to the firm</li>
<li>Aspayment to the next of kin.</li>
</ol>

i) Partner shares only profits and not losses since he didn't participate in decision making that may have caused such losses.
ii) The liability of the minor is limited only to the amount of capital contributed to the business since any liabilities arising may not be part of his decision making.
iii) The minor partner can act on behalf of the partnership and such acts shall be binding on the other partnership iv) When the minor partner attains the age of majority he/she has up to six months to decide whether or not to continue with the partnership. If he/she decides to stay, he has full responsibility for and right to amayor partner.</p>

<li>The partnership's unlimited liability, which lead to losing personal property in the event the partnership business cannot settle its debts.</li>
<li>The agency burden, where every partner is an agent of the partnership, and one's partner's mistake, may affect the rest.</li>
<li>Limited managerial skill, may lead a minimum agreement of the business.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incorporated-business-joint-stock-companies">Incorporated Business / Joint Stock Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incorporated-business-joint-stock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-incorporated-business">i) Incorporated Business<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-incorporated-business" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>We have so far looked at unincorporated business and have seen the main features of such business as that they don't have a separate legal existence from the owners.</li>
<li>We shall now focus on business units that are legally viewed as separate and distinct units from the owners.</li>
<li>Such businesses are called in co-operated or joint stock companies.</li>
<li>Incorporated business organizations are legally separate and distinct from the owners or members.</li>
<li>The main form of incorporated business or joint stock company include:</li>
<li>i) Companies</li>
<li>ii) Co-operatives</li>
<li>iii) Public co-operation</li>
<li>These are advanced forms of companies where a group of people pull their savings together and contribute a scapital to setup a business enterprises or companies.</li>
<li>These companies are governed by Act of parliament, underthe Kenya's joint stock companies fall, underthe Kenya Companies Act = (cap 486) of 1948</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mainfeatures-of-jointstock-companies">MainFeatures of JointStock Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mainfeatures-of-jointstock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ As alreadynotedajointstock companyis anassociationofpeoplewho contribute capitaltoformcommon stockin orderto carryonabusinessactivityforproduct motive.
☑ Thecompanyformedcomprises-corporatestatusandisregisteredunderthecompany'sact.
☑ Ajointstockcompanymaybepublicorprivatecompanyanditsmainfeaturesinclude;
a) Legal personality – the company has identities separates from that of other personscontributing capital and can therefore hold property, contract in its own name sue andbesued.</p>
<p>b) Thesharesaretransferable-theshareholderscanselltheirinterestingthecompaniestother persons willing to invest in it (freely for public ltd company but limited to the consentoftherest oftheshareholders forprivatecompany.
c) Common sill – as a separateentity it will be necessary for a joint stock company to signdocumentsandsuchsignaturesarenormallyembodied inacommonsillofacompany.</p>
<p>✓ Thesilliskeptundercustodyofthe responsibleoffices.</p>
<p>d) Members/shareholderscannotbindthecompanybytheir Acts
e) Individual/ members are not entitled to take part in business since it is managed by the boardofdirectors
f) Shareholdershavealimitedliability.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dissolution-of-public-corporations">Dissolution of Public Corporations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dissolution-of-public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Since formation of a public corporation is by an Act of parliament it follows therefore, that in order to dissolve such an organization one would have to repeal the Act of parliament under which they are allowed.</li>
<li>The following reasons may lead to repealing the Act of parliament under which they are formed.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Perpetual operation of the corporation of a loss</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="typesofcooperativesocieties">TypesofCooperativeSocieties.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#typesofcooperativesocieties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acooperativeisavoluntaryassociationofpersonswhocometogethertopromotetheirsocialeconomictinterest.</p>
<p>Thetypesinclude:-</p>
<p>a) Producercooperatives
Aproducercooperativeisanassociationofproducersuchassocietieswhichcollect,process,marketanddistributethemembers produce.</p>

<li>Poormanagement caused by the system of choosing the managers. I.e. AGMelections.</li>

<li>Withdrawals are easy which may cause instability and discontinuity.</li>

<li>Lack of secrecy since all activities must be approved by all members.</li>
<li>Largenembership may cause management problems.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sourcesofbusinessfinance">SourcesofBusinessFinance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sourcesofbusinessfinance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Theentrepreneurmayobtainfinancefromthefollowingmain sources.</p>
<p>○Debtfinancing  ○Equityfinancing
○Externalandinternalsources.</p>
<p>☑ Debt financing requires a borrowing system and the entrepreneur is bound to pay back thefundsborrowed togetherwith interestpayable.
☑ Debt financing can be long term or short term. Depending on the lender collateral, amy berequired.
☑ Equity financing does not require collateral and offers the investor some form of ownershippositionin thebusiness.
☑ Internalfinancingarefundsgeneratedfromseveralsourceswithinthecompany,theyinclude profits sale of Assets, reduction in the working capital accounts receivable, retainedprofitse.t.c
☑ External sources of finance may come from family members, credit suppliers, governmentprogrammes,grants e.t.c.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="equityfinance">EquityFinance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equityfinance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Itthelargestsourceoffinancetoabusinessorganizationandusuallyformsthebaseofwhichotherfinances areraised.
☑ Equityisthetotalsumofthebusinessordinarysharesplustheretainedearningsalsoknownasrevenue reserves.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-ordinaryshare-capital">a) Ordinaryshare-capital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-ordinaryshare-capital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-using-debt-financing">Advantages of using Debt Financing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-using-debt-financing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Most debt financing is short-term and as such it will not burden the company's cost of financing for longi.ecost is short-lived.</li>
<li>Interest on debt is at a valuable expense and thus the effective real cost of debt will be equal to interest less tax on interest i.e. interest is less by the much of tax on it. (refer to cost of finance)</li>
<li>The principal is later reduced in real monetary values by much of inflation on it i.e. the company pays less on long-term loans by virtue of inflation reducing the real monetary value of the principal and interest.</li>
<li>The use of debt financed oes not necessarily entail dilution of control to existings shareholders are these shareholders may only lose the control if the company has used 67% of debt finance in its financing i.e. in its total capital employed.</li>
<li>It is usually invested in viable ventures whose return is higher than its cost, thus it is used with a good investment policy</li>
<li>This finance does not call for a lot of formalities in its use in as much as it does not involve a lot of flotation costs.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-debt-finance">Characteristics of Debt Finance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-debt-finance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>It is a fixed return finance i.e. interest on debt is fixed regarding less of the profits made by the company.</li>
<li>Interest of debt finance is a legal obligation on the part of company topay and failure to pay it may lead the company into receivership in the extreme.</li>
<li>It is usually given on conditions and restriction sex c.e. proffer overdrafts.</li>
<li>It carries a first claim on profits and assets before other finances.</li>
<li>It does not carry voting rights and as such it does not participate in the decision making process of the company.</li>
<li>It is user is est the company's gearing level.</li>
<li>It is always refundable except for irredeemable debentures.</li>
<li>It is usually a secured type of finance.</li>
<li>Interest on debt finance is a tax-allowable expense.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="similarities-between-debt-finance-and-ordinary-share-capital">Similarities between Debt Finance and Ordinary Share Capital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#similarities-between-debt-finance-and-ordinary-share-capital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>In the case of irredeemable debentures both for manper manents or c.e. of finance to the company</li>
<li>Both carry explicit cost to the company I.e. interest on debt finance and</li>
<li>Dividend on ordinary share capital.</li>
<li>Both are raised by financially strong companies</li>
<li>In case or irredeemable debentures both will entail a permanent cost to the company.</li>
<li>In case the company has used overdrafts then both are not secured finances.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classificationsofdebtfinance">ClassificationsofdebtFinance.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classificationsofdebtfinance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-short-termfinance">1. short-termfinance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-short-termfinance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This ranges from 1 month up to 4 years and is given to customers known to the bank or to lenders. The agreement of this loan will mention both the repayment of principal and interest, and mustidentifywhetheritissimpleorcompoundinterest.Forprincipal,ithastobepaidoversometime.This finance usually secured and the terms of the loan will be restrictive. Usually be invested in anarea acceptable to the bank or lender. Usually this finance should be used to solve short-term liquidityproblems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-medium-termfinance">2. Medium-termfinance.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-medium-termfinance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This finance will be in the business for a period ranging between 4-7 years. This term is relative and will depend upon the nature of the business. This type of loan is used for investment purpose and is usually secured but the security should not be sensitive to the company's operations. The financeobtained must be investigated while respecting the matching approach to financing i.e the term and pay back period must be matched. This type of finance if the most popular of all debt financing because most of the business will need it both in their growing stages and also their mature stages of development.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-long-termfinance">3. Long-termfinance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-long-termfinance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is a rare finance and is only raised by financially strong companies. It will be in business for a period of 7 years and above. This finance is used to purchase fixed assets in particular during the early stages of a company's development. It is always secured with a long-term fixed asset. Usually land or buildings. Its investment, however must obey the matching approach. In all, the companies needing such financed not have to be known to the lenders.</p>
