<p>Reasons why long term loans are difficult to raise on Kenya’s financial markets/ limitations of using long-term debts.</p>
<ol>
<li>This finance calls for long-term securities such as land and buildings which most businesses in Kenya may not have.</li>
<li>There are no long-term savings to back-up these loans due to low income of average Kenyaans and as much most of the savings are short-term and cannot be made available on long-term basis.</li>
<li>Most businesses in Kenya are agro-based and these are risky and as such lenders cannot avail their financial contributions as of long-term.</li>
<li>The central bank has tended to stimulate the development of money markets that capital markets which have not been fully developed to avail such finance to meet the development need so find a strong commercial sector so the economy.</li>
<li>Long-term loans are not usually profitable because interest and principal repayment are eroded by the bythe impact of inflation and thus banks may be reluctant to give such.</li>
<li>Theseize of the businesses in Kenya is small and such businesses are not going to concern so as to be able to attract this finance on long-term basis.</li>
<li>A number of companies in Kenya are multinational companies which obtain long-term finances from parent companies abroad and this has limited the development of capital markets in Kenya as demand by such companies is low.</li>
<li>There are been a tendency by the financial institutions to avail long-term debt for building purposes and little attention has been paid to long-term finances for businesses.</li>
<li>This finance is given on conditions and restrictions which make it less ideal for profitable ventures as such restriction may reduce profitability of companies concerned.</li>
<li>This finance is given on conditions and restrictions which make it less ideal for profitable venture as such restriction may reduce profitability of companies concerned.</li>
<li>Long-term forecasts by commercial banks are inaccurate and filled with a lot of uncertainties thus the banks are very reluctant to shield such potential risks and preferred short-term which they can forecast with some degree of accuracy and certainty.</li>
</ol>
<p>Solution to the above problems.</p>
<ol>
<li>The government should diversify the security such that the same asset acquired acts as its insecurity and also to allow guarantees as securities in particular personal guarantees.</li>
<li>The government or individual commercial banks should undertake mass education campaign to businessmen so as to induce them to save/keep their money in bank so as to avail such money of long-term lending.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-billsof-exchange">Disadvantages of Billsof Exchange<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-billsof-exchange" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factoring">Factoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This can be defined as an outright sale of the company's debtors to a factor (which is usually a financial institution that specializes in purchasing of debtors) this factor will pay the selling company up to 80% of the face value of debtors and is left with 20% to care of bad debts if any, and also his discounts, this type of source of finance is rare in Kenya mostly because it is an expensive source of finance due to high discount costs. Savings in this source are in form of costs of credit management which are transferred to the factor. However, the factor takes up risks in debts (of default) which previously were supposed to be borne by the selling company.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-why-factoring-is-not-popular-in-kenya-disadvantages">Reasons why factoring is not popular in Kenya (disadvantages)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-why-factoring-is-not-popular-in-kenya-disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-using-factoring">Advantages of using Factoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-using-factoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The selling company can obtain ready finance from the factor which can be used to solve its liquidity problems.</li>
<li>The selling company transfers the risk of bad debt to the factor company thus reducing its losses.</li>
<li>It minimizes the burden of collecting debtors' i.edebt collection expenses.</li>
<li>This finance can be raised fast thus does not entail a lot of formalities.</li>
<li>It does not carry collateral security thus a flexible source of finance to raise.</li>
<li>It can be raised by any company regardless of its status as long as it has good debtors i. e of reputable companies.</li>
<li>It does not affect the company's gearing level thus not loss of control to the company by its use.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="creditcard-buying-plastic-money">CreditCard buying (plastic money)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#creditcard-buying-plastic-money" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

Usually repayment carries interest charges. These cards are used to obtain such goods and services as:</p>
<p>i) fuel expenses in particular for tour companiesii) stationeryiii) Medical expenses for employee sand their families.
iv) Vehicle maintenance v) Air transport vi) Purchase of input such as oils, spare parts e.t.c.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="debenture-finance">Debenture Finance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#debenture-finance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by dspop Service Delivery (<a href="mailto:dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Debenture has its origin in the latin word Deboe which means “I owe” it is a document that is evidence of a debt which is long termin nature, and confirms that the company has borrowed aspecific sum of money from the bearer or person named in the debenture certificate. Most debentures are irredeemable thus forming a permanent source of finance to the company. If these are redeemablethenthesewillbelong-termloanswhichrangebetween10-15years. They can be endorsed, negotiated, discounted or used as securities for loans. They carry a fixed rate of interest with repayable after six months i.e. twice a year.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-debentures">Classification of Debentures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-debentures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-classification-according-to-security">a) Classification according to security<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-classification-according-to-security" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>i) Secured debentures - these are secured against the company's assets or have a fixed charge against the company's assets. In the event of the company's liquidations, such debentures will claim on any or all of the company's assets not yet attached by other secured creditors. A debenture holder with a floating charge has a status of a general creditor, however floating charge debentures are rare and they are sold by financially strong companies.</p>
<p>ii) Unsecured (naked) debentures - these carry no security whatsoever and such they rank as general creditors. They carry a residual claim to the first class creditors but as a superior claim to the first class creditors but as a superior claim to the first class creditors, but as a general creditor.</p>
<p>These are rare sources of finance and are sold by financially strong companies with a good record of dividend payment to the share holders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-classified-according-to-redemption">b) Classified According to Redemption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-classified-according-to-redemption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>i) Redeemable Debentures - these are bought back by the issuing company. Like preferences, these have two redemption periods which are minimum and maximum redemption periods. This usually between 10-15 years. i.e. the company has the option to redeem these after 10 years but before expiry of 15 years. In most cases redeemable debentures are secured against specific assets e.g. land or buildings (mortgage debentures) their interest is a legal obligation on the part of the issuing company.</p>

<p>ii) Irredeemable debentures (perpetual debentures) these can never be bought back by the issuing company except in the event of liquidation and as such they form a permanent source of financial category. These debentures are rare and are only sold by financially strong companies which must have had some good dividend history. These are unsecured and thus are known as naked perpetual debentures.</p>
<p>c) Classified according to convertibility.</p>
<p>i) Convertible debentures - these are the type of debentures which can be converted into ordinary share capital and this conversion is optional as follows;</p>
<p>a) Atthe option of the company, e.g. the company’s option.
b) Atthe option of both parties, e.g. debenture holder and the company
c) Atthe option of the holder.</p>
<p>However the conversion price of the debenture is given by</p>
<p>i) Conversion price = nominal value of the debentures
No. of shares received</p>
<p>ii) Conversion ratio = <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mtext>Nominal&nbsp;value&nbsp;of&nbsp;debentures</mtext><mtext>Nominal&nbsp;value&nbsp;of&nbsp;share&nbsp;to&nbsp;be&nbsp;converted</mtext></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{\text{Nominal value of debentures}}{\text{Nominal value of share to be converted}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2251em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8801em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">Nominal&nbsp;value&nbsp;of&nbsp;share&nbsp;to&nbsp;be&nbsp;converted</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">Nominal&nbsp;value&nbsp;of&nbsp;debentures</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span>
In all, convertible debentures are never secured.</p>
<p>iii) Non-convertible debentures — these cannot be converted into any shares but ordinary or preferences hares and are usually secured.</p>
<p>d) Subordinated debentures (naked)</p>
<p>These are issued with a mutuality period of 10 years and above and usually they carry no security and depend upon the goodwill of the company. They are so called subordinate because they rank last in claims after all classes of creditors except trade creditors. Nevertheless their claims are superior to those of shareholders both preference and ordinary shares.</p>

<p>Advantages of using Debenture Financeto Ordinary Shareholders.</p>
<ol>
<li>The use of debenture finance does not dilute the shareholders control of the company unless they are convertible and are converted.</li>
<li>Under boom conditions ordinary shareholders may benefit from higher dividends due to fixed charges on debentures which is paid under condition of high profits.</li>
<li>Interest on debentures is tax-allowable expense and as such this may allow the company to retain more and even pay higher ordinary dividends to its shareholders.</li>
<li>In case the company issues irredeemable debentures, these will be invested in long-term ventures with not only have the effect of raising the shares pieces of the company's ordinary shares but will also increase the company's future ordinary dividends.</li>
<li>After debentures are redeemed, the company will benefit from the asset/investment they had financed which will increase the net worth of shareholders.</li>
</ol>
<p>Trade Credit</p>
<p>This finance is obtained by companies by which purchase goods on credit and pay for such goods later. This "kind" and is available to companies which can pay bills on time as and when they fall due. It the largest source of finance to sole traders and wholesalers in Kenya. This is cheap source of finance and it does not entail any explicit cost except discounts foregone. This finance may be long-term in particular if the company meets its bills regularly such that after settling a given bill the same company obtains further credit immediately, thus may become a continuous source of finance. In order to be a source of finance, credit received must exceed credit given.</p>
<p>Advantages of using trade credit in Kenya a source of finance (reasons why trade credit is popular in Kenya)</p>
<ol>
<li>Most businesses in Kenya lack collateral securities which are necessary to raise other forms of debt to financial resources to trade credit.</li>
<li>It is cheap source of finance because the only cost involved is discounts lost, enough to increase the price to trade credit.</li>
<li>Most other finances need the borrower to maintain healthy accounts which small businesses in Kenya may not have thus resort to trade credit.</li>
</ol>
<p>Page 106</p>
<p>Downloaded by dspop Service Delivery (<a href="mailto:dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>The fact that small businesses in Kenya are not known to lenders makes trade credit the best source of finance as they may not qualify for other finances which require that the borrower be known to the lender.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-limitations-of-using-trade-credit">Disadvantages (limitations) of using Trade Credit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-limitations-of-using-trade-credit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The debtor company will undergo the opportunity cost of the discount foregone by the very buying company.</li>
<li>This finance is not reliable because in the event of default on the buyer's side the seller cannot give it and this way cut the buyer's credit line which may lead a lot of inconveniences and in some cases stop pager in production or sales of the debtor.</li>
<li>It is usually restricted to working capital items and as such may not be available for fixed assets which are important for profitability reasons.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="promissory-note">Promissory Note<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promissory-note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ A promissory note is a bill wherein one party promises to pay another party on a specific date and conditions, a specific sum of money. It is a short term source of finance to the company, usually up to 3 months. This type of finance is used when the two parties know each other well. It acts as a source of finance in as much as it can be discounted or endorsed. It can also be used as security for loans.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-and-disadvantages-promissory">Advantages and disadvantages promissory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-and-disadvantages-promissory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="invoice-discounting-confidential-factoring">Invoice Discounting (confidential factoring)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#invoice-discounting-confidential-factoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an arrangement where the selling company discounts its invoices usually with a bank or financial institution and will receive a large percentage of its invoices in cash in advance. Usually it is expensive source of finance and should only be used if the company cannot obtain overdraft finance from commercial banks. The invoice discounter analyses which invoices to discount and in this case he will request the selling company to send original invoices to the customer and a copy to the discounter. The invoice discounter has not only lien on the debts but also recourse to the borrower in which case the seller or borrower will have to pay the discounter’s should any debt or default to pay his bills on the due date.</p>

<li>the hiree has a lien over the asset until the final installment is cleared in which case if the hiree defaults the hiree may repossess the asset in particular if the hiree has not paid 2/3 of the value of the asset this will entail a capital loss to the hiree once the asset is repossessed by the hiree.</li>
<li>It may be difficult to get a guarantor for expensive purchases e.g huge machinery as their value may be beyond the financial capabilities of a number of guarantors making it difficult to acquire heavy fixed assets necessary for the company’s operations.</li>
<li>By not purchasing the asset outright, the hiree foregoes discounts which will be an opportunity cost as a result of hirepurchase.</li>
<li>Hire purchase is limited to those assets which are available with the hiree and as such may not cover all areas of the company’s financing need, e.g. for working capital.</li>
</ol>
<p>Institutional Investors</p>
<p>✓ These are body corporates which avail finance for long term use, and avail their finance through purchase of shares in the stock exchange, debentures and through mortgage finance to deserving financially strong companies. Companies that avail this finance include trustee companies, pension organizations, insurance companies, and investment companies’ e.t.c. these avail finance in large quantities and usually doths to earn a return on the same finance or to acquire ownership in those companies so as to safeguard their investments. Companies which are financially strong will attract institutional investors.</p>
<p>Advantages of using finance from institutional investors.</p>
<ol>
<li>it is cheaper to raise this finance because it will be available in large sums and from a few companies i.e. flotation costs will below.</li>
<li>These institutions using their financial experience can advise the company in its investment activities so as to utilize such finance more profitably.</li>
<li>the cost of servicing their finance is low as these will be paid with a few cheques unliket he case with a company having a large number of shareholders with will issue many cheques this increasing the cost of servicing this finance.</li>
</ol>

<li>These investorswill come to the rescue of the company permanentfinance if theypurchaseordinarysharesand this willbeusedin longtermventures.</li>
<li>Being major shareholders they will contribute valuable ideas during the annual generalmeetings and such ideas may improve the running of the company benefiting from suchfinance.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4efd713">3. The company’s gearing level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4efd713" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ The gearing level will influence the company’s ability to raise further finance in as much as highly geared companies are viewed as highly risky as they have used more debt finance than equity finance. This exposes it to chances of receivership and consequently liquidation as creditors can recall their money at short – notice. This means that high gearing will not allow the company to raise debt finance as creditors will be reluctant to lend to a highly geared company. Also such a company cannot raise equity finance as the demand for its shares will below due to such indebtedness.</p>

<p>Definition: a business plan is a document that convincingly demonstrate that your business idea can sell enough of its products and services so as to make products and services so as to make satisfactory profit and attract able to potential financiers.</p>
<p>In other words, a business plan in a road map you can follow to start and manage a successful business. It shows step by step on how to start, fund, manage, monitor, and evaluate a successful business.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="business-ethics">Business Ethics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#business-ethics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Ethics: this is a set of moral principles that govern the action of an individual or group</li>
<li>The principle should play a significant role in guiding the conduct of manager’s entrepreneurs and employees in the operation of the business.</li>
<li>Business ethics is concerned with the right and wrong in the practice of entrepreneurs (business)</li>
<li>It addresses both the body of principals governing business practice with emphasis on the product the consumers and the entrepreneur’s moral concepts.</li>
</ol>

<p>Important Aspects of Business Ethics</p>
<ol>
<li>Competition
☑ Competition is regarded as healthy and fair when carried on within acceptable business limits as established by business principals, manners and values.</li>
</ol>
<p>Unfair competitive aspects
i) Reduction of prices of goods and services to every low levels with the object of putting competitors out of business.
ii) Explaining the ignorance of the consumers as on quality and quantity.
iii) Grouping together with a view of lowering the prices in order to push other out of business.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aspect-of-management-ethics">Aspect of Management Ethics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aspect-of-management-ethics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>

<p>Discipline</p>
<ul>
<li>The term discipline simply means that members of a group confirm to the rules andregulationsframed byanorganization</li>
<li>Discipline is the orderly conduct of affairs by the members of an organization whoadheres to its regulations because they desire to corporate harmoniously in forwardingthe end which the group has in view, and willingly recognized that, to do this, eitherwishes must be bought into a reasonable union with the requirements of the group inaction.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="codeof-ethics">Codeof Ethics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#codeof-ethics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The term ethics refers to a general idea or belief that influences people's behaviour andattitude.</p>
<p>A code of ethics refers to a set of laid down moral rules or principles which govern behaviour ondeciding on what is right and what is wrong,</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Ethics from the foundation of the people of an organization as theymakedecisionsorinternallyandwithotherstakeholders</p>

<p>EthicalBusinessPractices</p>
<p>✓ Ethics is a major factor in the social responsibility of business. Ethical philosophy if abranchoophilosophythatisconcerned with the judgment of the rightness of wrongness of an act. The aim of professional or business ethics in the protection of professionalism, human rights, integrity of character, and good service. In general, the issues considered in such code of ethics consists of;</p>
<p>a) Honest—in this respect, it is necessary that facts are presented fairly and accurately. Claims made about products or services, even in the</p>
<p>b) Fairness — every one whom you deal with should be given appropriate consideration. This includes workers, customers, suppliers and others with whom the organization interacts.</p>
<p>a. Loyalty—this is interms of loyalty to other stakeholders, e customers,</p>
<p>b. Workers, n suppliers’ e.g.</p>
<p>c) Confidentially — this is especially important for service industries such as banks. It is important that transactions with customers are respected and protected so that they are not disclosed to third parties.</p>
<p>d) Trust—there should be a mutual trust where the owners of a business should have proper trust in their customers, while the customers should also have enough trust in their organization. Without trust, no meaningful and lasting relationship can develop.</p>
<p>e) Courage—this refers to the need to treat others with respect, be incorruptible in business operations, even when it means losing the business</p>
<p>There are four main schools of thought in moral philosophy, offering different approaches to solving ethical dilemmas. These approaches are ways of an organization forming their code of ethics. They include</p>
<p>Page 149 of 165</p>
<p>This document is available on studocu
Downloaded by dspop Service Delivery (<a href="mailto:dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">dspopservicedelivery@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>a) Deontology- this is the ethics of principle equating any decision with a moral law. This principle maintains that the act itself should be considered in judging the rightness of an act. For the “normal idealist” the motives of the actor and the a consequences of the act should be ignored in such judgments. This means that any act is right if it is consistent with an accepted moral principles or law. Societies have developed certain rules that members generally accept e.g. people do not rob or deliberately injure each other. These rules are valid in many situations including organizational ones.</p>
<p>b) Utilitarianism – this is the most deliberate of the three approaches. It maintains that the rightness or morality of an act lies not in lies not in the act nor in the motives of the act and deems it right if majority benefits. According to utilitarianism, if the consequences of an act to the individual and society, both the good and the bad, represent a net increase in society's happiness, then the act is good.</p>
<p>c) Teleogy- this is the ethics of purpose. It considers whether the outcome of an action accomplishes the original goal. It uses the actor's motives in determining whether the act is right or wrong. It gives priority to the individual to judge the action. If an act which is within the law ensures the continuation of the business, then it is right.</p>
<p>d) Egoism: this is the ethics of self-interest, claiming that personal or organization benefits are the only rational criterion for judging economic actions.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="e-government">E-Government<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-government" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ E-Government is a new term that finds wide applicability. While the term still means different things to different people, available evidence suggests that it had been undergoing progressive conceptual development. So for the three generation: the ir conceptual development that have been identified and discussed below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-first-generation-conceptualization">1. First Generation Conceptualization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-first-generation-conceptualization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Page 152 of 165</p>
<p>✓ In this conceptual generation, e-government is conceived as the government equivalent of e-commerce, and used to mean the application of advanced ICT to deliver government services. This conceptualization emerged from the relative success of “e-commerce” applications resulting in pressure being placed on government organization were doing. As a public sector equivalent of e-commerce, e-government is viewed primarily as a tool for electronic delivery of public services. The government transfers a range of services into electronic formats so as to make them more conveniently accessible over the internet.</p>
<p>✓ Proponents of this conceptual view include Douglas Holmes (2001), Negaham Cook (2000) and John (Arrow 2001). According to Holmes “electronic government or egovernment, is the use of information technology, in particular the internet to deliver public services in as much more convenient, customer-oriented, cost-effective and altogether different and better way. He further points out that cutting costs, and improving government efficiency, meeting and improving citizens expectations and relationships and facilitating economic development are some of the important considerations driving government.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="features-of-e-government">Features of E-Government<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-of-e-government" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) It is smart government in the sense that it selectively used of variety if ICT in ways and are as to add value.</p>
<p>b) It is customer-driven in that, customer needs and conveniences drive its organizing structures and business processes.</p>
<p>c) It is responsive, transparent and accountable, respondents to the need of its customers, and employs ICT to support continuous engagement with customers.</p>
<p>d) It is available on a 24*7 basis (24 hours a day and seven days a week.) thus it does not kept its customers waiting for office hours and working days.</p>
<p>e) It is accessible from any where since it is ICT-enabled.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-e-government-is-not">What E-Government is not<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-e-government-is-not" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ E-Government is not simply about technology; it is about the applicants of technology specifically ICT, in government.</p>
<p>E-government is not so much what the government does but it is about to want to complete its tasks</p>

<p>✓ To protect the local industries, existing industries and employment, every country tries to protect them. This is done by two ways.
✓ One, by fiscal regulatory measures like, hightaxation, inspection, monitoring controls, quantitative restrictions and foreign exchange controls. Second through non-monitoring barriers like introduction of controllers and inspectors, large documentation, legal insecurity, social and cultural barriers and treatment of outsiders in a different way as compared to insiders.</p>

<li>Entrepreneurial culture</li>

<p>✓ An entrepreneur should be open to consider dispassionately the business opportunities that are coming in other countries. The entrepreneurs should have a wide vision to expand geographically.</p>
<p>Advantages of an entrepreneur going global.</p>
<p>✓ Largemarkets beyond home country borders
✓ Greater motivation in new opportunities
✓ Improvements in the technologies, quality and operations
✓ Extending life of product cycle
✓ Challenges in doing business in competitive environment
✓ Earning foreign exchange for the organization and home country.</p>
<p>Social Cultural Trends</p>
<p>✓ The social cultural environment of a business consists of class structure, social mobility, nature of social organization, social institutions, customers and taboos. People’s basic beliefs, values and norms are largely shaped by their society.
